COURSE: Chakra Healing
AUTHOR: Anodea Judith

Preparation

========================================

Preparation 1: What is Chakra Healing?

We have a paradigm in which mind is separated from body. We have a paradigm of separation. People are divided within themselves. They are living in their heads and they're trying to have mental concepts to fix that, but the body is ailing. They're going to doctors to fix the body, but they don't look at the spirit and what's going on. I'm Anadeya Judith, author of Wheels of Life and a number of best -selling books on the chakras. I've been a spiritual teacher and a therapist for over 40 years, and I've traveled the world seeing people and their problems. People get lost in the spiritual smorgasbord. They're dedicated to their growth, but there's so many paths in so many ways, and they don't know quite how to put it all together. They don't have a systematic map for their personal growth. And that map is the chakra system. It's been my life's work ever since. So a chakra is an energy center. It's like an organ in the energetic body. Just like we have a heart that's an organ in the physical body, we have these organs in the energetic body. And they organize energy, they organize the life force through four functions. Through the receiving, we receive love, we receive information. Through the assimilation of that, can we absorb that? Can we store it? Can we remember it? And can we express it? So we take in, we assimilate, we store and we express and each chakra needs to be able to do all four of those functions on each and every level. Most people think of the chakras as this ladder that they climb up to higher consciousness. And that indeed is what it is. That's one of the pathways. But I discovered there is an equally powerful current that comes down through the chakras. It starts in highest consciousness with an idea. And then we visualize that idea. We imagine it. We speak about it. We give it words. We fashion our sound bites. And we find the right relationships to bring that vision into being. We empower ourselves to get done what we have to do. We move things into place. And the thought planes get denser and denser until in the first chakra, they manifest on the physical plane. That's the current of manifestation. The densifying, if you will, of thought, step by step in a practical pattern. That's beautiful. I never thought about it that way. Seven chakras to me describe the architecture of the soul. And just like a body worker or a yoga teacher might study the physiology, as a psychologist, I've studied the soul. And I found that it has this architecture that is basically the same for everyone and yet has an individual expression for each person. This chakra healing quest is a 35 -day journey. into the deepest core of yourself. We will work with all seven chakras and we'll spend three days on each chakra with one on the mind and our psyche and how we got programmed by childhood experiences, one on the body with yoga and bio energetic exercises to condition your body, and one on spirit, how we can address the larger universal experience and address what's happening in the world. It's a way of connecting heaven and earth, mind and body, spirit and matter, back into an indivisible whole, something that will bring you powerful, dynamic, permanent change.

Preparation 3: Fundamentals: Introduction to Chakras
--------------------
<v ->So today we're going to learn the fundamentals</v> of the chakra system. We're going to have an overview and look at all the chakras together. So first of all, what are the chakras? Well, most of us know them as energy centers but what does that really mean? I'll give you my definition. Chakras are wheel-like energy centers, and the word actually means wheel, that's what it translates as, for the reception, the assimilation, the storage, and the expression of life force energy. You could think of them as chambers in the temple of the body and just like the chambers in your home, you have a kitchen and a living room and a bedroom, each chamber is designed to receive a different kind of energy. When you come home from the grocery store, you put your food in the kitchen, you don't take it to the bathroom and that kitchen is designed to handle the food, it's designed to let you prepare it, assimilate it, eat it and place to put the garbage so you can take it back out. So each of these chambers in the temple of the body is designed to handle a particular kind of energy and how we receive it, assimilate it, store it, or express it has to do with the health of that chakra, so as we're healing our chakras, we're bringing these aspects into balance. The chakras also relate to levels of consciousness, ways of looking at the world, like a lens, looking at your survival issues, your emotional issues, your power issues, your relationship issues, your communication, your imagination, your wisdom, looking at all these different aspects of your life as different levels of consciousness. They're metaphors. You may not believe that there's any kind of energy systems in your body at all, but it's a very profound philosophical system that is a metaphor for various aspects of your life and the world and really, it's a map to the architecture of your soul. So just like we study the bones and the muscles and ligaments and organs of the body in order to better understand the body and how to keep it healthy, we also have an architecture to our soul and if you really want to heal the soul, you have to understand that architecture. So everybody's talking about chakras these days, but where did it really come from? Some say it's from ancient India thousands of years ago, but there's nary a mention in the very oldest documents of India. You could maybe extrapolate a little bit here and there but the real teachings came around the tantric period of Indian philosophy. That was maybe 500 to 1200 AD, depends on what scholar you talk to. So there were texts written about the chakras, from that period of time in history. The Shatchakra Nirupana, the Padaka Pancaka and the Gorakshashatakam was written in the 10th century. Many of these texts were translated by a man named Arthur Avalon, or Sir John Woodroffe and this was one of the first books published in English called "The Serpent Power" published in 1919. And in those texts, the chakras were points of meditation, they were areas of the body or elements that we meditated upon, there weren't a lot of postures that went with it and they were just something to guide your meditation, but the chakras describe a very profound, philosophical system. They have locations in the body and through that, in the modern updating of the system, we look at the elements in each chakra, earth, water, fire, air, and in the old texts, it says ether, but I've extrapolated it to a seven-element system, sound, light and thought or consciousness. We look at these elements, we look at where they are in the body, what that part of the body is doing and from that is created a full philosophical system that looks at your life. Now as a psychologist, I also looked at this from the psychological point of view. I saw what came through my office in my clients and in my students and my teaching and the issues they had and what their history was and I started to put this together, survival issues coming from this part of your life, power issues coming from that part of your life. And as I started to put that together I could see a whole psychological schema. and as people have worked through that in my book, "Eastern Body, Western Mind," people have transformed and had amazing results. People tell me that every day. So I know that there's viability to the psychological aspects of the chakras and that's what we bring to you in your healing. Now, I've also been a yoga instructor and chakras come from the yoga tradition. And yoga means yoke, it's the way to link the mortal with the divine, like yoking a horse to the carriage. And that yoke of yoga, to me, the chakra system is the structure of the yoke of yoga. It is the architecture that shows how the mortal body is yoked to the divine through these seven steps. So these are a map for the personal journey. So the word chakra literally means wheel or disc and I'm sure it's not what the ancients meant, but think of your chakras as programs on a floppy disk. Remember those? Each chakra contains core programs that govern everything you do, feel and think. If you want to change your life, you need to change that programming. You need a systematic step-by-step plan, for both liberating yourself, from fixed forms that hold you back, and for manifesting your higher ideals. Chakras are a map that can help you connect to the organs in your physical and energetic body. For example, if you're stressed, it might be an imbalance in your third chakra, which governs energy, power and will. Anxiety can be too much energy, depression can be too little. This is ways that that chakra can get out of balance. If scarcity is an issue and you feel like there's never enough, maybe that's a core program in your root chakra that governs survival. If you want to open your heart, well, that would be the heart chakra. If you want to balance your relationships, if you want to open your communication and free up your creativity, that would be your throat chakra. By changing your inner world, you change your outer world, because really, the chakras are portals between the inner world and outer world at seven different levels. Some healing systems like Western medicine, address primarily the body. Others look at mental health and address the psyche and are devoid of the body. Some systems are spiritual, like meditation or yoga, but they don't necessarily address the psychological elements. To me, the chakra system is about the only thing that addresses all three aspects, body, mind and energy, or body, mind and spirit and puts them together in an indivisible whole. And many systems of healing are already here but they don't really address changing the culture, they're all about just working on yourself which can become narcissistic after a while. I mean, if you look at 30, 40 years, of people doing spiritual work and what a mess the world is in, it's obvious there's something else we need to do, we need to bring that learning back down. Well, chakras are not only a guide for your personal journey, they're a guide for humanity's evolution. How do chakras work? A chakra is a vortex of energy spinning at the core of the body, but chakras are also portals between the inner and outer world and they have gates that act as defenses to keep things from coming in and also to keep some things from coming back out. So they're gates that mediate between the inner and outer world and those defenses slow down what we can receive or what we can get rid of and result in blocks in the chakras. We mentioned how chakras contained programs, well, programming starts at birth, if not before, and some of our programming is conscious, like the language we speak and the things we believe and primarily most of it is unconscious programs that govern our behavior and thoughts that we don't even know were there. Our purpose here is to make the unconscious conscious so that we can have a choice about it. That's part of the liberating current. So the content of these programs is formed by our history, by the things we've been taught, the things we've gone through and experienced, how we dealt with that, what our defenses were that allowed us to survive the slings and arrows of childhood. They've taught us what we believe, and they have put those programs into our nervous system and even the structure of our body. The trouble is we have bugs in the programs and sometimes we need to upgrade those programs to get them to work in a modern system, just like we do when we upgrade systems in our computers. So what are chakras made of? Ultimately, they're made of energy. Energy that in yoga is called prana, in martial arts or Chinese medicine it's called chi or qi, Freud called it libido, Star Wars calls it the force, Wilhelm Reich called it orgone energy, the word that I use in this Quest is charge. I like to think of charge as standing for consciousness having a really genuine experience. And charge is something we can all relate to, but all of these words refer to the same thing, they're the system of energy in the body and that's what chakras are really designed to organize and handle for you. Now, these energy centers are aligned along the core of the body. In yoga that's called the sushumna, the central channel that goes from the base to the spine and it's the central integrating channel for all the chakras, but it's not the only one. There are spiral currents that go crisscrossing through the chakras called the Ida and the Pingala, which means moon and sun, respectively, and they crisscross between the chakras and meet at the sixth chakra and at the first. There are also currents through which energy travels. There's energy meridians that we know from Chinese medicine and in yoga they call them nadis, lots of subtle currents and they say there's 72,000 nadis in the body that carry and generate energy and prana and carry it to the body. Part of our job is to purify those nadis so they can carry the energy more effectively into and out of the chakras. And then finally, there's this force called Kundalini, which is said to be a goddess in serpent form that spirals and undulates up and down your spine to pierce and awaken each chakra in turn. We won't be trying to generate Kundalini in most cases, we're trying to clear the chakras so that if Kundalini should arise, your chakras can better handle it, and we'll talk more about this when we get to the crown chakra. In addition, we'll be traveling to different currents up and down the chakras. When we go from bottom to top, we're going from earth which is fixed, to water which is more fluid, to fire which is even freer, to air which is invisible, to sound which can travel through space, to light that can travel from a distant galaxy, to consciousness that's everywhere. We're moving from the finite to the infinite, we're getting freer and freer as we rise. This is the current of liberation, in the old texts, it was called moksha or freedom. So we liberate ourselves from fixed patterns and become freer and freer. This is the bulk of our Quest. At the end of the Quest, we'll be taking the downward current, the manifesting current that begins with an idea or a thought or an intention and then we visualize that and we bring it down into a little bit more concrete form. Once we've seen it in our mind's eye, then we talk about it and that's even more concrete. We bring it down into the heart, we find the right relationships, we empower it with action, we move things into place and move along and finally, we bring everything together in a fully manifested form. This is the manifesting current. Now, in the old texts, it was called, Bukti, which means enjoyment. So it is through the descending current that we enjoy the manifestation that is a condensation of consciousness, getting denser and denser at each level and coming into physical form. That's the other side of the journey. So one thing about these upward and downward currents is as they go through the core of the body, you can imagine that like roundabouts in a highway, they are creating a vortex of energy. Why do we have to heal our chakras? Well, we can't complete the liberating current or even the manifesting current if we have blocks in our chakras. So we have to clear them, give them what's necessary for them to function well, clear out the old, unuseful programs, the limiting beliefs, the things that get in our way so that the liberating current can complete its journey and take us to higher consciousness and freedom and the manifesting current can choose what it wants to create and create it and bring it into full form. How do our chakras get blocked? Well, you can think of a block as when the manifesting current that originates in consciousness is working counter to the liberating current that is coming up organically from the body. So let's take an example. Let's say you have a job and there's somebody you work with that really, maybe it's your boss that you don't like and they make you angry. So every day you come in, organically, you kind of feel this anger, this annoyance, but you say, "Oh, if I let that out, "I'm going to lose my job." So you have to be nice, so every day this comes up and every day something comes down and then they meet and they block, so you can think of it as two opposing forces. What we want to do is harmonize these two currents, let them complete their journey all the way up. Now, does that mean you get angry at your boss? Not necessarily, but if you acknowledge that anger and you can let it out in a different way and you can acknowledge why you want to be nice to your boss, then you have a harmony between the two currents. So you can think of the blocks also as knots, K-N-O-T, where in Sanskrit, it's called granthis, knots of resistance that the energy can't quite get through. But I like to think of those knots as N-O-T, it's where you are not, where you cannot, where you will not, where you do not, where your have not, and what we want to turn all that no and negative energy into something positive. We want to break through the knots and make it a yes for you in your life. Well, chakras as energetic centers, will respond to what happens in your life and when you feel a threat, your energy may increase in order to deal with the threat, or it may scare you so much you say, "I'm out of here," and you want to avoid the threat. Well, that creates an excessive coping strategy or a deficient coping strategy. You're either compensating or you're avoiding. So you may have a deficient heart chakra that just doesn't want to deal with relationship. Or you may have an excessive heart chakra that needs to be the center of attention all the time. Or you may have an excessive third chakra that has to be powerful and controlling, or you may have a deficient third chakra that's weak and passive. So when we look at the blocks, we're looking at what kind, and in this diagnosis, comes the treatment. An excessive chakra needs to get rid of energy or charge. A deficient chakra needs to take it in and charge up, it needs to expand and really receive and hold and store that energy. And so when we talk about chakra balancing, we're balancing the excess and deficiency in each chakra, we're also balancing between the chakras. You may have one that's deficient and another that's excessive, and you want those to be balanced with each other or balance your upper chakras with your lower chakras. So what does it mean to heal a chakra? Well, we're working with balance between excess and deficiency, but we're also working body, mind and energy and spirit altogether. So you may have created body armor as a result of a particular chakra. We want to clear that, we want to stretch those muscles, we want to discharge some of that. You may have programs in your psyche that influence your behavior and what you think. We want to clear the unproductive patterns of the past and replace them with new, more productive patterns. We want to mend some of the wounds of childhood that get lodged in the physical, emotional, and mental programming. So we're going to be clearing past traumas, that get lodged in the psyche, we're going to be balancing energy flow in the body, we're going to be looking at behavioral patterns and shifts that we can make to change our habits, we're going to align the chakras as a whole system, and we're going to learn how to work with energy and move energy through the body into different parts. And since chakras work with energy and energy is everywhere, we're also looking at it, not just inside ourselves, but outside ourselves, and healing the spirit. The spirit is something universal that we all share and you heal your own spirit as you heal some of the issues that occur in the world as a result of our wounded chakras. So your exercise for today is to look over the chakra charts in the workbook, some of the associations. Assimilate your understanding of the chakra system with other things you may have studied. Maybe you've studied the Kabbalah, or maybe you studied Chinese medicine, see how they go together. Look at your self-assessment and see which chakras need particular work, those are the ones you're going to want to be sure and not miss those lessons in the schedule. So download week one of the chakra companion workbook and get excited about what's to come, look at what you can do. Share any aha moments with the Tribe and ground yourself, fasten your seatbelt, we're getting ready for takeoff.

Preparation 4: Meditation for Chakra Activation & Intention Setting
--------------------
<v ->Before the start of any journey,</v> it's important to know why you decided to take this Quest. It will be helpful for you to revisit the information later when the journey gets rocky, if it does. So think about who do you want to be by the end of this journey? It starts from your intention. Think of it in the positive and think of it as already here. "I am centered and focused. "I am happy with my life. "I am living in abundance. "I am grounded. "I am peaceful. "I am awake." Set that intention, put a stake in the ground. We're going to learn more about clarifying intention in the manifestation current, but for now, start with the end in mind, that's one of the secrets to success. So next I'm going to lead you on an opening meditation in which you get to visit all your chakras. So set yourself up for a meditation position with your spine erect and prepare to go on the ride. Chakra opening meditation. Close your eyes and settle into your inner world. Open to this moment. Open to this place you are sitting. In your body, here on planet earth. Allow yourself to witness your breath coming in and out easily and effortlessly. Your presence in this moment. Alive, aware. So there's a certain holding that gives us stability in order to grow. Now in order to grow tall and reach the heavens, we need deep roots. You don't go out to your garden and say, I'm going to help the flowers get high faster by pulling them up by the roots. We need to put them down deep. The dirt needs to be held around the roots. So stand upright. Your feet hip width apart. Or even shoulder width apart. I find most people bring their feet too close together. Turn your heels out a little wider than your toes, and soften your knees so your bending your knee out over your second toe. Ideally you would see you big toenail right on the inside of your kneecap, that is, if there's no clothing or anything in the way. And now press down and out with your feet as if you're trying to push apart two floorboards, or you're trying to stretch a sticky mat that you're standing on. And notice how your ground really hooks on. How is really grabs hold. How your base becomes more stable. If someone were going to push you around from this place, they'd have a harder time doing it. So that's the grounding stance. Now to charge it up, inhale and bend your knees a little bit more, keeping your shoulders over your hips, and as you exhale, push down through the core of each leg. Push down and out with your feet, and very slowly begin to straighten your knees, but don't straighten them all the way. Maybe 90% of the way. Then inhale and bend again. Inhale deeply, press those knees down, and exhale. Press down and out through your legs as if you're pushing the floor away, and the result of that is your legs begin to straighten, but it's a slow movement. Come to about 90% of the straight. Don't lock your knees, then inhale again, and go back and forth, inhaling and bending, exhaling, pushing through the core of each leg. Now if you're doing this correctly, you're going to start to feel a little bit of trembling in your legs, and that's a sign of charge or energy coming up your legs. That's what you want. Inhale, your hands up over head, and reach higher to the heaven while bending your knees, taking your tailbone behind you, and slowing bringing your arms forward, reaching from your tailbone out to your fingertips. Pull your shoulders back, lift the chest , and press down and out with your feet. Inhale and come back up. Inhaling, your hands up over head, straightening your legs, reaching once more , and on the exhale, take your arms down around your side, place them on your hips, and bend forward all the way, keeping your knees bent and wrapping your arms around your thighs, bringing your belly as close to you thighs as possible. Give your legs a hug. On the inhale, press your knees back until you find your edge, then release your hands. Take them into the floor. Straighten your legs and inhale halfway up, extending from the tailbone to the crown. Deep breath in and then lower back down. Hands on either side of your feet, once again, honoring your legs that carry you on the journey. And the next breath in, take your right foot back into a high lunge, straightening the right leg, hugging the muscles to the bone and pressing your left foot into the mat and drawing it toward your right foot. Feel the stability that comes from anchoring into the ground. Take a breath here and slowly lower your right knee down to the floor, flatten your right foot, and gently bend your left leg, sliding your hands back, using blocks if necessary. As you straighten your left leg and flex the left foot, make some circles with your left ankle, clockwise and counter-clockwise, to exercise the foot and the ankle. And then with toes pointing toward the ceiling and the foot flexed, gently press your left heel into the mat, drawing the left leg up into the hip socket as you press your tailbone out behind you. Inhale and lengthen through the crown, and on the exhale keep that length as you slowly bow over your left leg. Go to wherever you find your edge. If you need to use blocks, that's fine. If you only touch your knee, that's fine. Press your tailbone out behind you, and then on the next breath in, lift your head, bend your left knee back out over the left foot, tuck your toes behind you, hands on either side of your front foot, and take your left foot back next to your right for a Downward Dog. On the next breath in, lower your hips, move your shoulders over your hands, bend your knees, take your knees, chest, and chin down to the mat. Wiggle the tailbone a little bit just so you feel it, and then lower your hips and just with muscles of your back, do just a Baby Cobra, lifting your crown, hugging your legs towards each other, and on the exhalation, lower back down. Tuck your toes in behind you, press your hands into the floor, press your hips back up once again for a Downward Dog. Stretching into your Dog, wiggling each knee, pressing into the four corners of your mat, anchoring into the ground. On the next breath in, take your right foot up between your hands, bending your right knee, and slowly lower down onto your left knee, flattening the left foot. Place your hands on your block, or slide them along the floor as you slowly straighten your right leg. Flex your right foot. Make some circles with your ankle, clockwise and counterclockwise, pointing and flexing the toes. And then with your toes pointed straight up and your foot flexed, press gently into your right heel, hugging the right leg into the hip socket, and lengthen through your tailbone and your crown. Inhale , and as you exhale, keep that length as you bring the center of your torso down over your right leg to wherever you find your edge. Just pause at that edge and allow your breath to so gently move you. Maybe a quarter of an inch with each exhale, without strain, pulling the roots down out of the base of the spine. If muladara means root support or foundation support then you want to give support to others, you want to get support from others. Look at what is the support system you have in your life. So the name of this chakra's Svadhisthana. Means one's own place. So one of the challenges in this stage is to be connected with your own place inside, to be in touch with yourself. And that is a feeling state, that we feel comfortable in our own skin. We feel comfortable in our world. And when we feel comfortable, the energy flows through unencumbered. That's how we gain an emotional literacy that later on, we can identify what we're feeling and express it appropriately. We also want to establish an emotional connection with our caretakers. That's something that we feel. We feel good in our mommy's or daddy's arms. We feel good in our home, that everything is humming along as it should be. And then our feeling state is denied, and we're knocked out of our own place. Some things that cause blockages is as we're moving into our environment, is the bulk of what we experienced pleasurable or painful? If it's not a safe environment, if there's a lot of anger, or violence, then we're going to restrict our movement and we're going to have trouble moving out and moving forward in our lives. We're also speaking the emotional language of the family. If your family was very expressive and volatile, and emotions were flying around the room, that's what you learn to speak. If your family was very reserved and nonemotional, then you might not have learned to speak that emotional language very well. So that has to do with some of the programming of your second chakra. So if this stage doesn't go well, or some of these things that cause blockages happen, what happens to us as a consequence? Well we get out of touch with our own place. We get out of touch with each other. In a culture that denies the feelings, that denies pleasure, that denies sexuality, we're a culture that is getting rapidly out of touch. And we get out of touch with ourselves, we don't even know what we feel anymore. And our emotions become unbalanced, and the charge of our emotions become unbalanced, and the chakra becomes unbalanced. We may overindulge as a result of not having a pleasurable life. Well I'm going to eat that cookie, or I'm going to have that drink. We may deny ourselves pleasure, and then we're just not feelin' very good most of the time. So excessive would mean too much water, too much emotion, too much feeling, we're pulled off our center by being carried on waves of tumultuous emotion. Some people only feel alive when they're really feeling intense emotion. Well that's an excessive second chakra. It could also be overly indulgent. On the other hand, if we went to an avoidant response and developed a deficient second chakra, we might be very flat emotionally. We might not know what we feel or feel anything. Life is kind of dry, and dull, and boring. It's just not fun and juicy anymore. And we feel out of touch with ourselves. Now people always ask me, can I have a little bit of excess and deficient in the same chakra? And the answer is yes. And especially in this chakra, which is both emotions and also sexuality. Some people are highly sexual and not very emotional, some people are highly emotional and not very sexual. So these are like petals of the chakras. Some of them are trying to compensate, some of them are trying to avoid, and they're always that we were just trying to come into balance. So what does a balanced second chakra look like? Somebody who is fluid, who is sensuous, who is feeling their feelings appropriately, not too much, not too little, someone who's really in touch with themselves, in touch with other people, and really feels the world within them and around them. So another thing that happens when the second chakra is compromised is we develop guilt. We feel guilty about what we feel. Oh, I shouldn't feel that way about this person, or I shouldn't want this, or I shouldn't need that, or I shouldn't have this sexual fantasy. And guilt stops the flow of energy. Now if you've done something wrong that hurts somebody, it's probably appropriate to feel a little guilty about that, and to apologize and make amends. But I know with myself, the demon of guilt comes up if I do my practice in the morning and I take a nice long meditation and yoga practice, I feel guilty that I didn't get to my desk sooner. And if I skip my practice and I go straight to work, I feel guilty that I didn't do my practice. So one day, I just said to myself, what's with this? This is just the demon of guilt acting on me instead of me really choosing, what do I want? And coming from a place of choice in my own body. So the challenge of guilt can hinder the natural flow of emotions and desires that is part of this second chakra. So if we remain wrong for what we felt or we were punished, we might get caught into very binary either-or-thinking. It reflects the duality of this chakra. We might think things are black and white, good or bad, right or wrong, but the fact is, nature is much more nuance than that. It comes from fear of punishment, that we want to get it right, we want to have it absolute, but that doesn't allow us to feel our way. That comes from the head. So next time you get caught in either-or-thinking, try to just feel the nuances of the situation. Go down into your second chakra, and go, what feels right to me? And try to feel the nuances in between those polarities. So when you master or overcome this pervasive sense of guilt, you can enjoy whatever you're having more fully, whether it's a cup of tea, or a meal, or a sexuality, or a sunset, you can enjoy it with your senses more fully. And this is not to say that we can do anything we want without guilt, it's not about that overindulgence, that's an excessive second chakra. We want to have an appropriate flow of feeling in the body and with that, you harvest the gift of extreme pleasure and delight in the world. When we can't feel, we restrict that movement, we restrict that fluidity, and then the nourishment of the energy doesn't flow through the body, it doesn't get to the other chakras. To get from solid to liquid, how do you get there? You melt. So as we melt our rigidity, as we melt our fixed patterns, we come into more of a flow, we have a river of energy inside us that can flow through us and nurture any part of the body in any of the chakras. To not have to necessarily spend it in the expression of that emotion, but not to have to stuff it and block it either. To take feeling as a kind of information coming from the body to take you into your wholeness. So stop and notice what you feel, notice where it is in your body. Notice what it makes you think about. Even just that starts to heal some of this disconnection from the self that puts us out of touch. And for those on the medium track and want to take this deeper, notice where your feelings may have gotten lost in the first place. What was the emotional language taught in your family? What were you taught about your feelings? Were you allowed to feel and express your emotions? Was there anybody there to meet you and support you in those emotions? Anybody there to hold? So just do an inquiry. There's questions in your workbook to reflect and take this deeper. When you feel an emotion come up, pull back from the story of that emotion. The story of oh, this person hurt you, or they didn't listen to you, or they insulted you, or whatever happened and instead feel the charge of that emotion in your body. That charge is trying to move and flow. Notice where the charge is, and notice where it isn't. Notice where you might be blocking its movement. Regard whatever created that emotion as the situation that is giving you a gift to come home to yourself and your own charge by feeling what goes on in your body. We think it's dominating other people. That it's owning more money. That it's having more dominion. But that disempowers us because what empowers one is disempowering another. And that just creates more -isms in the world. A warrior tribe is going to have a new model of power, a model of power with. When we have domination of one part over another, whether it's one race over another or one country over another or one gender or even one part of yourself taking power over another, that implies separation. But real power comes when we put things together. When we join together. When we cooperate and collaborate and work together towards something new. But we have to reclaim our own power in order to do that effectively. When we grow up in powerlessness it actually creates a love of power. We say, I don't want to be dominated like that, so I'm going to grow up to have power. And then, we do it just like everybody else and we dominate, and that's not what we want to do. Part of growing up is to take full responsibility. To join our power with each other to empower ourselves as individuals and each other as a collective. We've lost the sense of our power within, of our own sacredness. We've lost contact with that, and instead of seeing outer authority as the source, we need to see inner authority as a resource. Real power is gained by cooperation, integration, and purpose and wholeness. So, one thing about taking your power. It isn't necessarily safe. No one can guarantee that you're going to not be accosted, that you're not going to be challenged, that you're not going to be made wrong. Imagine this story. Let's take an average guy, we'll call him Carl, who wants to go to Central Park in New York and sit on a park bench on a Saturday morning. He's sitting there enjoying the sun when all of the sudden a uniformed guard stands in front of him and blocks the sun. Well, Carl, being a pretty nice guy that doesn't want to make waves just sort of moves over on the park bench and goes back to sitting in the sun. Well, the uniformed guard moves over in front of him. Carl says, excuse me. And the uniformed guard takes his hands and pushes Carl back down on the bench. And Carl, getting a little more angry now, says hey, I was just minding my own business. I was just sitting in the sun. And the guard steps on both of his feet and holds him down. And now Carl's really irate. And the uniformed guard takes a chain out and chains him to the bench. And then, all of the sudden Carl looks around the park and he sees all these people chained to their benches, and they're all scowling at him for making a fuss. So, you have to realize, what would you do in that situation? And does that happen to you? Are you the one that raises an objection at work and everyone else makes you wrong? Well, sometimes the person that rises up and takes things in a new direction, it isn't easy. Not everybody appreciates it. The people who have not claimed their power can make you wrong, so you have to really own your power and your integrity and stand by the responsibility of all the actions that you take. What's the antidote to this powerlessness? Well, we have to live from integrity. We have to have integrity in everything we think and do so that we can stand by, with responsibility, all of our actions. We have to heal the notion of power, that the notion of power is to do good in the world, to help people, to make change. We have to reward that instead of the power over. We have to bring integrity into all our actions. Rainbow warriors operate from a set of values. Power isn't something we do alone, that's the old paradigm. We have to join with others, get support from others, collaborate, cooperate, see what we can create together. Take risks, take a chance, see what happens. It may not be as bad as you think it is. You may be able to step out, and as you do and fly by the seat of your pants, you develop that muscle of power. Create a new definition of power, one that inspires and strengthens rather than diminishing others. Live by that definition. Let your actions be in that definition and inspire others by your actions, set an example. After all, it's up to us to change the world. So, the spirit practice is two parts. One is to define your values. To live from integrity and find out what's really important to you. There's a core values list in your workbook that you can look at to see for reference and inspiration on what your core values would be. Then live in alignment with your value system. Once you identify with your values, then bring your actions into alignment with your value system. Exercise choice and you exercise your will. There's an exercise where you can look at four columns. Something you commit to, an action that you want to take. Third, who does that action benefit? And fourth, can you mark it off as accomplished, that you did it? Column B is your purpose. How does that align with the values that you've chosen? So, in your workbook circle your top five values. Write it down in your journal and use at least one of those to complete the integrity exercise. Share what you're doing with the tribe and inspire someone else, set an example, and lead the world. So, now we've done three full chakras. Tomorrow we go up into the heart.

So we're going to explore all these things today as we explore the heart chakra psychology. So what's the purpose of the heart chakra, in this great scheme of things? Well, it's to expand beyond ourselves. The third chakra and our power is basically egocentric and there's a place for that, we need to know who we are and what we're doing in life. But then the upper four chakras get beyond the ego and when we do we open to something greater. We just go around with an open heart but not wide open to just anybody, it still has discernment but it's centered and balanced and that love radiates outward. <v ->Welcome back to a topic today</v> that is near and dear to my heart. And that's taking the global perspective of the heart chakra. We're going through a huge paradigm shift on this planet. That we started as cave dwellers working close to the earth, we learned to build ships and have agriculture, and through farming, we could expand. Instead of being organized by power over, as I mentioned in the third chakra, we're working with power with. To take care of the environment, to take care of each other, and create a new world that I call the waking of the global heart, a new organizing principle. If we care for ourselves, we are better vessels for making change in the world. So what does it really mean to care for something? It's to consider it, to look at what it needs, to see what would make it better. Caring for your children is seeing that they're fed and they're loved and they're supported. Caring for your garden means that it's watered and weeded. We do what it takes to care for things. Now you might say in this world today with so many things wrong that you get what we sometimes call caring fatigue. Oh my goodness, it's the rain forests, and it's the people, and it's the oceans, and it's the climate, and it's the economy, and all these things to care about, which one? I like to quote Andrew Harvey who says that, "Whatever is most breaking your heart, "that's where your service lies." If you wake up in the night worrying about the rain forest, or sex-trafficked children, or the rape culture, or the people who don't have enough to eat, that's where your service lies. And when you do that service you may find the heart really sprouts wings. There's an uplift when we get beyond ourselves and give to something greater. We become something greater. So the exercise for today is that sometime in the next 48 hours, do something unexpected as a favor for someone else. You know, mow your next door neighbor's lawn, or buy some flowers for somebody at work and just put it on their desk anonymously. Give a little bit more to a beggar on the street. You know, instead of givin' him 50 cents, give him 20 bucks. And see what that feels like in your heart. Pay somebody's coffee forward when you're standing in line and they're behind you. Just see how that lifts your heart. And if you're a person that has caring fatigue, in other words, you go, "Oh, I do things for other people "all day long, and I'm exhausted," then do that same act for yourself. Buy yourself a little goodie, take yourself out on a date, have a little extra sleep in the morning, and do some unexpected favor for yourself. See what that feels like. So love begins at home in our own hearts. When our heart is filled, we radiate it outward. And that makes love contagious. Wouldn't that be a nice thing to catch from each other? That's how it spreads. And tomorrow we go into review and integration.

Heart chakra meditation. Close Your eyes and bring your attention to your inner world. Find your alignment by pressing your roots down into the earth and lifting your crown up to the heavens. And another breath in to this glorious air. For air is the element of the heart chakra. We take it in, we let it out. And peace and balance. Allow your breath to deepen, taking in even more air, more expansion, more uplifting. And on the out breath, let everything soften. Let your face soften. Let your shoulders soften your hands. Let your chest soften soft like a feather, soft like a pillow, soft like a baby's skin. We soften the boundary between inside and outside, and we allow the breath to come in and out as if it was breathing through every pore in your skin. Inhaling love in with a breath and exhaling love. Back out. A simple give and take. Always another breath there to take. Always one to let go of. And an another breath in its wake. And as we take in that breath, it's the breath of the universal. It has no edges or boundaries, no differences. It accepts. It just simply is nothing to do, nowhere to go, but just to be, To love, to open. Everything around you is in relationship. Everything is giving and taking in perpetual balance, so much is provided for you. Are we grateful enough for all that is given to us? Open your heart to the gratitude of even just this precious breath. It fills your heart with love and lets it out with peace, connection, Fullness, Acceptance. Accepting yourself just as you are. A perfect being held in a web of unconditional love, like a mother holds a child. Even when the child stumbles, she knows he will walk. And this unconditional love holds you even in your trials, holds you in compassion, holds you like a baby, knowing that you are finding your way, finding your way to love, to open, to forgive, to soften, and to accept all the blessings that love can offer.

Roll back down to the mat one vertebrae at a time. Take a deep breath in, hug your knees into your chest. Roll back and forth again and roll back to a squat. And then lift your hips for a forward fold. And now take your right leg back to a high lunge. Firming up both legs, left knee out over the left ankle. Find your stability and lift your torso upright, raising your hands up overhead, interlacing your fingers, turning your palms to the ceiling, taking your head back once more, sound. And then pressing your hands toward each other, bring them down your core. Take your right elbow to your left knee and twist. Lengthen between your right heel and the top of your crown. Take a deep breath in, perhaps another sound. And then release your hands, take them to either side of your front foot. Bring your back foot forward. And lower your head . Shake your head loose. Shake your head yes. Shake your head no. Shake your shoulders, I don't know. And then press into your feet, tuck your tailbone, rise back up. Interlace your fingers overhead one more time. Turn your palms up to the ceiling, take your head back. And then slide your hands down your crown bringing your palms together, bring them to your heart. And end this with a nice om. Om. Now that you've done the yoga, let's just look at some everyday movements you can do in a few seconds. So one is when your neck gets tired, especially you've been sitting at your computer for awhile, just kind of take your head and roll it around, stretching the neck on each part. If you go to one side, you might take the opposite hand and pull your ear down towards your shoulder a little. The free hand can then massage some of the muscles on your neck. You can take it to the back and you can take the other side, do a little massaging up and down. And that helps to relieve some neck tension. Shake your head side to side and just loosen it up. Another one to work with, the tensions that happens in the jaw from clenching your jaw and closing your throat chakra is that if you take your hand or even someone else can do this to you and put it under your chin and then open your mouth and make a sound so you're pressing against the resistance of your hand. And that means your jaw muscles have to go the other way and open and that's a good way to release jaw tension. For the next 24 hours, practice tuning into your body, how it feels in your throat chakra whether you say something or whether you don't, how you might tense up when there's something important to say. Use any of these movements that we've shared with you. Today we looked at letting sound out of your throat chakra and tomorrow we will explore the cost of remaining silent.

LESSON 17 - Throat Chakra: Healing the Spirit by Connecting to Larger Truths
--------------------
<v ->Welcome to healing the spirit of the throat.</v> You know, it's not enough just to do our own work. We're all singing a symphony together. We're all creating a new world together. Our truth wants to be expressed, and your truth is necessary. Speaking our truth changes the world. It connects us to larger truths, and there is a big cost to remaining silent. Remaining silent allows the status quo to stay in place. When there is fear, guilt, shame, grief, even lies, it allows lies to prosper. People will believe anything, because we're not speaking our truths. Now, sometimes we think, good boys and good girls are silent. We're obedient. We don't want to make waves. We have to give up our need for approval and safety, and sometimes, speak truth to power. Let people know how you feel, let people know, especially, when you do that, what you would like, how you would like it to be better, what's your idea for change? Express that. We can see how the world is very disharmonious. There's horns honking, and trucks going by, and bells ringing, and, phones ringing, and we're constantly bombarded by sound. And we get out of harmony. We get out of resonance with ourselves. That's why quiet time, and meditation, and listening to music can be so important. Rhythm is actually an organizing principle, not only for the body, but for society. Look at what happens when a whole crowd goes to hear a concert. Music is part of every spiritual and revolutionary movement we've had that is successful. Creativity brings us artists. Artists are often the social architects of a new world. They create the leading edge of culture. We can demonstrate and make phrases that catch on as sound bites. We can create new possibilities by uttering them into existence. So dare to break out of your mold. Dare to break out of your silence. Dare to be creative. Speak your truth to power, and take it into a movement. So how do we become as Rainbow Warriors, speakers of the truth? How do we become change agents through our communication? Well we have to change ourselves from the inside out. And we have to learn methods of clear communication. If we had tools of communication, we could work things out, instead of going to war. So, learn techniques of mediation, diplomacy, how to listen, how to do active listening and reflect back what you hear from someone else. Learn to speak in the "I" voice, meaning you're sharing what's inside you, rather than telling the other person you're doing this to me, or you didn't do that, or you did do that. Say, I feel this inside. You can follow the lines of non-violent communication by Marshall Rosenberg that has a very good and simple model for creating clear communication that creates intimacy. As we learn each other's language, we learn each other's ways, and we create a more global community. And of course, we have the tools of global communication through the internet and our cellphones, where we are tuned into what's happening all over the world, instantaneously, through the realm of constant communication. So they say we have two ears and one mouth, because listening is so much more important than speaking. Imagine a world that really listened, where we could hear the truth of everyone, and create a symphonic chorus of creation together. Another cost of withholding our truth, is that it creates distance in relationship. Whatever you haven't said to a friend, to a partner, to a co-worker, brings a little distance between you and that person. And usually what you haven't said might be something negative, sometime when you were hurt, or annoyed at that person, and, maybe you just didn't want to share that. Well there's a simple process created by Stan Dale of the Human Awareness Institute, for sharing those kind of things, and it's called The Withhold Process. So, Withhold is anything you haven't said to a person. It can be positive or negative, but usually it's negative. And you simply say to the person, I have a withhold that I haven't shared with you. Are you willing to hear it? This gives the person a choice. It lets them brace themselves that they're going to hear something, and they have the option of saying yes or no, and you have to respect that. If they say no, I just got home from work, and I'm really tired, I don't have the bandwidth to hear anything right now, you have to respect that, and you might say, well, is there a time, you might hear it tomorrow? But, you have to accept no is no. If they say yes, and, it's good to preface this process with them ahead of time, when you're not triggered, so, you preface the person on how to do this before you share, that they would only say thank you when you share your withhold. So then you can speak from yourself, and say, well last night, when you went to bed early, and didn't do the dishes, I felt, overburdened because I do the dishes all the time. You're not saying that person was wrong, you're not saying you never do the dishes, or you don't help around here. You're speaking of yourself, and you're just saying, I felt annoyed and disgruntled. And, the person simply listens and just says, thank you. And what they're really saying is, thank you for sharing your withhold. They don't give you a rebuttal, they don't say, but I do the dishes Tuesdays and Thursdays, they don't say, but I did them in the morning. They just say thank you. Now, later they might have a withhold for you, and, this process of sitting down with someone and sharing withholds, you'll find if you do it, and you do it carefully, brings you closer. Once you've gotten those things off your chest, you usually want to say something positive. And you know, I also forgot to tell you how much I appreciate what you do do around the house, or how much you take care of the kids, or, whatever it is that you appreciate about them. You find that comes out naturally, once the withholds have been shared. What if a person consistently says, no, they don't want to hear it, or that person's not available to talk to, or maybe they're not even alive anymore? Well, you can get a third person to sit in. Let's say, you want your friend Nancy to stand in for all the things you never got to say to your ex-husband. So Nancy says, well, tell me a withhold you've held back from George. And then you say, George, blah blah blah. And, Nancy just says, thank you. Tell me something without, tell me something else you've withheld from George. Well George, I never felt that you really heard or understood me. Thank you. Tell me something else, and they pull withholds from you, until you feel empty and discharged. And then, you don't have so much connection to these negative associations. You feel more positive toward that person, you're freer, you're more able to go on to the future, without being stuck in the past. So here's a reflection for today. Underneath everything you say, underneath everything you do, what are you really trying to say? See if you can listen for that, and see if what is the core communication? Are you trying to say, I can be helpful? Or, like me? Or, take me just the way I am? Try to listen for that. And in saying that thing you're always trying to say, underneath all you say and do, what is it that you're longing to hear? And how can you tell that to yourself? And that's a really good thing to share with the Tribe. Let's hear your inner voice. Let's hear your core truth. Let's hear what you're longing to say. And that wraps up our throat chakra. Tomorrow we'll move from speaking our truth to seeing the light and seeing clearly. See you there.

And then looking across a horizontal line, take them to the left as far as you can, and back to center. And down to the lower right. And back to center. Now we're going to lift our eyes up again without moving the head, and take them around the clock to the right, down below, up the left. Circle them around a couple times. And then back to center. And then once again lift your eyes upward without moving your head. Take them around the clock in the opposite direction, to the left and down, and to the right and up. A couple times, and then back to center. Then close your eyes and rub your hands together, creating some friction and some heat in your palms. And when you feel that heat in your palms, gently cup your hands over your eyes, and feel the warmth. So I mentioned how when we block off this chakra we often furrow our brow. So a nice thing to do is do a forehead pull. Take your four fingers along the midline of your forehead and press in and pull out toward the side of your head. Maybe a couple times. And then when you get to your temples, massage your temples. And then go back to the inner corner of your eyebrows. Really press, it's probably going to be a little tender, and pull, follow your eyebrows out, just massaging gently. And then I like to take it around to the bottom of the skull and just do a little tapping here. That's a good third eye stimulation. So the exercise for today, I call capturing light. If you go outside and you see light glinting off a windshield, or you see a very beautiful color, like a very red rose or a very pink shirt or something that is just a very rich green lawn, pause, take a breath, and really open your eyes to see it. Drink in that color or that light. Drink it in and nourish yourself with it. And look at it until you can close your eyes and see it in your own mind. So practice closing your eyes. Can I still see it? If not, I'm going to open it and look at it more. Drink. Close my eyes. Ah, now, I can still see the image of that red, red rose. You're depositing it to your inner temple. I've been doing this for a number of years, and I find that as I do it, my ability to visualize gets brighter, the colors in my dreams gets brighter, my imagination gets more intense. It's sort of like, if you put those colors on your palette, then you can use them in the painting. So nourish yourself with light. Light is a vitamin, just like vitamin C or protein or anything else that we need. We need light, and most of us are light starved. LESSON 20 - Third Eye Chakra: Healing the Spirit by Creating a World of Beauty
--------------------
<v ->We've now looked at the third eye in terms of the body,</v> and now we move into the soul. It's often said that the eyes are the window to the soul. Here, we look at creating and seeing a world of beauty. I think of beauty as a very underrated spiritual value, that when we see beauty, we know we're very close to the divine, and here, we're one step away from our ultimate seventh chakra, connection with everything. So being able to see is about opening to the big picture, and what an amazing picture it is, of how everything goes together, the world we're creating, to see through time and space, and even see our perspective from cosmology that we are this little speck of a planet, and one star among billions of stars in our galaxy alone. And then when you consider that they're now saying there are trillions, not billions, but trillions of galaxies, each with billions of stars as big as our own, that is an incredible expanse of universe that we are living in. And we are probably the only creatures on this planet that are capable of seeing out that far through our telescopes, and seeing into the micro through our microscopes, so our ability to see into past and future, large and small, is enhanced by this chakra. And so when we look at how this chakra is impacted by the world or how we can impact the world, it all comes down to creating a vision. I think people today, and societies in general, are floundering for lack of a vision. Most of what we have built came from a vision that was active at one time, and now we need a new vision, a new vision of what we can become at this time on the planet. We have the most amazing technology we've ever had, power is in the hands of the common people like never before, we can go where we want, we can say what we want, we can broadcast, we can create, and we can put this out and share among the millions. But what is it we want to create together? What is the vision of where we're going in the future? What is our evolutionary vision? That's what we want to create in this chakra. And then we want to use our throat chakra to tell a vision and broadcast that everywhere. When people come to a building site to work, there's piles of lumber and glass and nails and cement, they don't know what to do with it unless there is a blueprint, and the blueprint says, "This is the house we're building." And by that blueprint knowing what they're building together, each of the workers knows what to do with the materials they have. Well, in the same way, we need to be building an architecture of the future, we need to be making that architecture something that fits onto the human body and the human predicament and the human journey of its soul. So we talked about how illusion is the challenge of this chakra, and there's a major illusion that many people are under, and that is that we are all separate from everything else, that I'm separate from you, that we're separate from the planet, we're separate from the cosmology, one race or gender is separate from another, and we call that the illusion of separation. But as we come in to see the big picture, we see that we're really all one. Just think about when we first saw the pictures from the Moon landing of looking back at the Earth from space, there were no political boundaries of countries, it was just one single blue planet floating in space. Another way to think of this is to look at the ocean, each wave is individual, but each wave comes out of the body of the ocean, and each wave is connected to every other. So if you were just a little fish on the tip of a wave, you might think each one was separate, but as the wave goes back down, you realize this is all one ocean of creation and each one of us is rising and falling. So seeing, especially in the imaginative sense, is an act of creation. If you hurt yourself and you keep looking at your knee and you see it as whole and healthy, you're actually beginning to create that reality. Attention follows what we see, what we see is what we download. So where you have your gaze fixed, whether you're looking at the positive or negative, that all has an effect on what you are receiving and what you are creating. So begin to see something, even if it isn't there yet, to see the cities turning green, to see people being helped, to see a new world, and every day that you visualize that, you bring it that much closer to coming into being. So make use of your power to visualize. Instead of seeing roadblocks, turn them into stepping stones, opportunities, see them as possibilities for what you can create. Audrey Hepburn said, "It's not that we have the word impossible, "the very word says, 'I'm possible'". So see possibilities instead of roadblocks. So the practice here, as we come up into our sixth chakra, is a practice of becoming still. Imagine that your consciousness is reflected in everything around you, if you want to see the contents of your consciousness, just look at the world you've created, it's a reflection. Our general world is a reflection of our collective consciousness. But in order to see that reflection clearly, you have to be still. Imagine you're camping out in the wilderness, next to a big beautiful lake, behind which are mountains. If you wake up early in the morning and you sit in front of the lake when the lake is perfectly still, the surface of the water is like a mirror that reflects the mountains clearly, no distortion. As the ducks wake up and the boats come and the children swim and the wind comes up, there will be waves on the water, and then that image is broken up into pieces and you won't see so clearly. Well, all day long, there are things stealing our attention, saying, "Look at me, look at me, "look at this, look at that", and our attention becomes fragmented. So in meditation and in the act of stillness, we are quieting the mind so that the reflection we see is not distorted, we see it clearly. So if you want to come to clarity, allow yourself to come to stillness. So the exercise for today is to take some time and really come into stillness. And in that stillness, bring yourself up to your third eye, and take a perspective on something from outside yourself. Maybe you imagine being in another person that you're having conflict with, and imagine you're looking out through their eyes at their world. Maybe you're taking the perspective of someone that's very different from you, a different gender, a different race, a different nationality. Take perspective of someone you don't like and see what it looks like from their point of view. If you really want to up it, take a perspective from beyond this Earth or looking at the whole earth. What if you were a god or a goddess looking at the planet, what would you see, what would you change, what would you imagine? The more we expand our perspective, the more we expand our world and our understanding, the more we see the big picture. So that takes us through chakras five and six, the throat and the brow. Tomorrow is an integration and review day, and then next week, we will start our seventh chakra and our conclusion of the upward current.

LESSON 22 - Crown Chakra: Healing the Psyche by Surrendering Into Grace

<v ->Welcome to the seventh chakra,</v> our final step in the upward current. If you've made it this far in this course, congratulate yourself. You've done an amazing job to take in this much material in a short time so pat yourself on the back. And if you've missed a couple calls, that's probably normal and you're just jumping in at this point, that's perfectly fine. Make a point to go back at some time later and pick up on the chakras you missed. Right now, we're going to step across the threshold into the realm of pure consciousness. So your lower chakras are the stepping stones to your highest consciousness. We mentioned how roots that go deep allow the plant to grow tall, how those roots need to be watered and water needs to move all the way through, how we need to harness the sunlight, that's your power chakra, your fire, to bring that fire into the belly and into your core and how we want to blossom out from the heart and expand and soften. We attune in the throat, we see our way in the sixth chakra, but here's the question. Who is it that's doing all of that? Who is it that's living inside you, seeing out from your eyes, hearing these words right now, living in your body, running the show of your life, making your decisions? Who is that and how do you know? Ultimately, it's consciousness. It's consciousness that's doing all that, consciousness that sees, consciousness that hears and turns those words into meaning, consciousness that loves and feels the connection with everything else, consciousness that knows how to take action and what to do, consciousness that feels, and consciousness that is operating your body. So stepping into the seventh chakra is actually using that consciousness to examine itself, to examine your own consciousness, to be aware of your own awareness, and that near exercise is one that takes you into the thousand petals unfolding. So why is it important to come to consciousness? Well, all of the great spiritual movements from so many traditions are about realizing the consciousness that is behind everything. It's consciousness that's infinite. It doesn't take up any room. It doesn't take up any time. It can expand indefinitely. It's our consciousness that allows us to see out to the stars, to see inside us. It's consciousness that is operating and creating everything that we experience. If it weren't for consciousness, you wouldn't even know it was there. So what's the psychological aspect of the crown chakra? Well, this one is not so much about a developmental stage because we're constantly learning about the world, processing our thoughts, studying, taking in information, and making our own internal roadmap of the world around us. But there does come a time when we kind of graduate from childhood, when we grow up enough to leave home and go out on our own, and at that time, we begin to make our own worldview. It might not be the same one that your parents taught you. You might have a change in religious ideology, you might have a change in point of view, you're questioning, you're saying, who am I? What am I for? What's my purpose? What am I doing here? We question and we start to create our own worldview, our bigger picture, our understanding of how everything goes together. There's an enormous expansion of consciousness that happens through learning and that happens as we grow up and go out and explore the world. And as we do that and realize that it's consciousness that's running the show, then we want to develop techniques for expanding and refining that consciousness. But one aspect of our higher consciousness you might call higher power. This is where we can download some piece of wisdom or guidance. It seems like it comes from something beyond ourselves. And whether you explain that to yourself as being from a god or a goddess or a spirit guide or just your higher mind, it doesn't really matter. We are reaching to something beyond some kind of grace and downloading it. And some people find that difficult to do which is understandable. Your first experience of your higher power was actually your parents. When you were a little infant and you didn't know much about the world, they were your guidance, they were your teachers, they were the ones who watched out for you and taught you what you needed to know. And if you couldn't trust that for some reason, maybe your parents weren't in the right mind or maybe it just didn't go smoothly or they didn't give you the guidance you needed, or maybe you didn't really trust their wisdom, then you might've closed off your crown chakra a bit to being able to download and trust that higher power. So maybe you go back to the sixth chakra exercise of blowing pictures and maybe doing some forgiveness in the heart, moving that image out of your way, and imagine a divine god or goddess as your parents and download a higher power from that. So another aspect of the consciousness within and the aspect of consciousness that we call the mind, which is not our only consciousness, but that the mind is busy interpreting your experience. The mind is busy making meaning out of everything that happens to you. So when you were growing up as a child and your mother was crossed with you or your father wasn't around much or whatever happened in your life, every time that happened, you took it to mean something and the meaning you gave yourself might have been mommy's having a bad day or it might be there's something wrong with me. That meaning may or may not be accurate but nevertheless, you took bits of meaning from your experience. We do this all the time and as we do it, we add up those bits of meaning to become beliefs. And if you thought I did something wrong so mommy's mad at me and you thought that enough times, you might say there is something wrong with me, I'm fundamentally flawed, and that becomes a negative or limiting beliefs. When we get to the manifestation current, we're going to show you a powerful technique for changing those believes. But right now, just begin to understand that meaning is the component of beliefs and though we want meaning in our lives, we have to watch out for what kind of meaning we take. So what does this chakra look like in and out of balance? Well again, you're not going to see too much physically but ask yourself, do you live up in your head most of the time disconnected from your body? Are you always trying to figure things out? Are you gathering information more than feelings? Do you have trouble keeping your attention focused? Are you overly spiritually attached to your purity? But if the chakra is in balance, you feel connected with something larger than yourself. You have the sparkle of intelligence, you're able to think for yourself, you're able to think clearly and learn things, you're in your wisdom and you're able to bring that wisdom into your life. So as we go from first chakra to seventh, we go from having one single body to a multitude of thoughts. We go from the finite to the infinite. And expanded consciousness wants to frolic in the infinite. And one thing that gets in the way of that is our attachments. You might say that's one of the challenges of this chakra. And while attachment might be necessary for making commitments and keep you focused in your lower chakras, you could be attached to taking care of your children for example or attached to showing up for your job, that's pretty normal, but there's other kinds of attachments that keep us from completing the liberating current. So maybe you're attached to what people are going to think of you, maybe you're attached to understanding why and figuring things out, maybe you're attached to looking good, attached to your youth. Of course, we know about attachments to people and pets and money and things, but there's all kind of subtle attachments.
